		<date>2011-12-27</date>
		<username>Steve Pulaski</username>
		<score>0.8</score>
		<shortDescription>Unholy night of eerie cinematography</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Black Christmas is a grisly and unapologetically gruesome remake adapted from Bob Clark's original 1974 controversial Christmas slasher. This one gets right what most remakes don't. It's not without flaws, but it surely pays more careful attention the formula and smooths out some of, what looked to be, the inevitable rough edges.For one thing, the film earns its R rating which is a blessing. I'm so very, very tired of PG-13 horror films and to see a remake of a violent slasher that was R rated be stamped with an R rating further shows that they didn't want to cut out all the gore to try and market to the teen demographic. Second, Black Christmas is more concerned with establishing a creepy and uneasy setting better than any horror remake I've ever seen. The cinematography is enriching and part of the reason the film still surprises me today. The music, which was the final work composed by Shirley Walker before her death a month before the release date of the film, perfectly enhances and compliments the setting to further the eerie feeling we get diving into this film blindly.The kills are some of the goriest in any remake I've seen. There's one scene, during the murder of the family, that could go down as one of the most disturbing yet well crafted scenes in horror in the last ten or so years. Black Christmas is mean-spirited and utterly proud of it. I've never seen such a shamelessly gruesome horror remake like this. It follows up every disgusting scene with one more of equal or more quality.The storyline is actually pretty well developed as well. It centers around Billy Lenz (Mann) who was abused and hated by his mother. After witnessing his father being brutally murdered then buried by his mother and her boyfriend, now his step dad, years later Billy, whom still scared, kills both of his parents and is now in a mental institution for the criminally insane. Every year he claims he'll be home for Christmas and tries to escape, but is caught every time.Now his home is a sorority house filled with foul-mouthed, attractive young women many of which you have to listen closely to pick up on their names. The actresses are played by Michelle Trachtenberg, Mary Elizabeth Winstead, Crystal Lowe, Katie Cassidy, Oliver Hudson, Lacey Chabert, and Kristen Cloke. Because James Wong is producer and many of the actresses were in Final Destination and Final Destination 3, films he worked on, I can only assume Wong was a big help when it came to cast this movie.The sisters spend their night opening their gifts, drinking, subtly insulting one another, and swearing the night away. Over the course of the evening, a man persistently calls them leaving harassing and eerie messages on the receiver. You can see where this is going...There is an involving story, some great cinematography, and a very interesting backstory. But the lack of character development is sad yet expected. The film doesn't really seem to concerned about the teenagers and surprisingly, without spoiling anything, there is less people alive than one would believe at the end. Which is why I think James Wong's role in this film was huge since the gory deaths and quick murders are very reminiscent of the Final Destination franchise. Black Christmas is brutal, vile, vicious, and true to its title, but also one of the artsiest horror films I've seen in quite sometime.NOTE: The star rating is pretty much void here. This could easily be given a one or a four. Stars don't shine on a black Christmas.Starring: Katie Cassidy, Michelle Trachtenberg, Mary Elizabeth Winstead, Oliver Hudson, Lacey Chabert, Kristen Cloke, and Andrea Martin. Directed by: Glen Morgan.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Ho-Ho-Ho Horror Redux of a Cult Classic</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>BLACK Christmas (2006) **1/2 Katie Cassidy, Michelle Trachtenberg, Mary Elizabeth Winstead, Lacey Chabert, Kristen Cloke, Andrea Martin, Crystal Lowe, Oliver Hudson, Robert Mann, Karin Konoval, Dean Friss, Jessica Harmon, Leela Savasta, Kathleen Kole, Cainan Wiebe, Christina Crivici, Howard Siegel, Peter Wilds. Ho-Ho-Ho Horror Redux of a Cult ClassicNot many recall the original 1974 cult classic horror film "Black Christmas" directed by Bob Clark ("A Christmas Story", "Porky's"), which featured Margot Kidder and Olivia Hussey, but the simple fact is "Halloween" as the first of its genre eclipsed the film as a holiday slasher film a few years later. The original is actually very scary and disturbing and the remake for the 21st century has its moments and wisely a few homages to its predecessor.Set in a snow bound Christmas Eve sorority row house with several of its inhabitants remaining and unknowing that the previous resident, a certified homicidal killer named Billy ? who killed his family 30 years ago ? has just broken out of the asylum and is making tracks for a sort of homecoming, sets the mood for this bloody good but by no means great remake with reservations.Namely the decision to give Billy a backstory. In the original the killer is never really figured out in spite of his trademark sick phone calls pranked on the nubile young women who anger him to the point of some truly nasty and twisted murders. The schizophrenic nature of the character is fleshed out to include incest and a twist that is best left unsaid, but for me I figured it out in the first few minutes of the film.Director Glen Morgan (who helmed "Final Destination") does a rather decent job with the bloodletting and heebie-jeebies, notably the use of eye imagery (the original had some trademark sequences of close-ups of the fevered maniac's eyeball peeping out of several holes) and the equally grisly come-uppances of the co-eds (who quite frankly are almost difficult to tell whose who since the majority are nubile brunettes; not necessarily a criticisms more than an annoying observation).While the chills and thrills are uneven at best the shocks come quick and deadly which is the way any genre fan will be pleased to hear. For trivia buffs Martin ? who appeared in the original as a victim ? returns this time as the mother hen to the sorority under siege.</fullReview>

These differences and changes are not for the good however. 		<shortDescription>Another dreary remake of a classic</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>It seems we live in a time where filmmakers would rather rip off a classic than come up with something original, and Bob Clark's 1974 classic Black Christmas is just another film to get the remake treatment - and rather unsurprisingly, not only is this film worse than the original - it's a damn awful piece of crap in it's own right. I won't profess to be a big fan of the original Black Christmas - although I like it better than Halloween and it probably would find itself high up on my list of favourite slashers...if I ever were to make one. This film would, of course, find itself propping up said list. Naturally, Black Christmas Remake takes place at Christmas time and focuses on a group of girls that live in a sorority house. However, it turns out that this particular sorority house was once home to Billy Lenz - a spree killer who murdered his mother and her lover years earlier after being mistreated. Naturally, he just happens to escape the mental asylum while the girls at still at the house, and soon they find themselves being tormented and picked off one by one by the demented killer.The first film was gritty like a slasher should be; whereas this one is all 'nice' and polished, like a slasher shouldn't be, and it really kills the atmosphere. We get introduced to eight young girls, which although played by some good looking actresses; are completely boring and very difficult to care about, which really kills the film. Black Christmas Remake is directed by Glen Morgan who previously directed the very decent remake of Willard. A director with only remakes on his resume isn't very impressive at the best of times; and much less so in this case for the fact that one of those remakes is this film! Aside from the young girls being killed, we also get 'treated' to the story of the killer, which is just as uninteresting as the rest of the film. There's a fair amount of gore, much of it quite grizzly, but again the polished look of the film makes it hard to be shocked by it. It's only short at just seventy five minutes, which is a good thing; though unfortunately, the director sees fit to pull an ill-advised twist out of his hat, which doesn't go down very well. As remakes go, this is surely one of the worst and anyone thinking of seeing it should get a copy of the 1974 film instead!</fullReview>

		<username>Prolox</username>
		<score>-1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>Awesome bloody remake!</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>I will admit when I first saw Black Christmas (2006) I didn't like it to well. Maybe it was because I had at the time, just seen the super creepy original that when I saw this one, not only was I disappointed, that the film lacked the creepy, scary feel of the first &amp; seemingly substituted a lot of the suspense &amp; tension of the original for out right blood &amp; guts, but also the fact that the film took a far more obvious approach in it's plot &amp; execution that I thought to myself "why bother?" however, upon recently seeing it again, it has now become one of my all time favourite slasher films! True, compared to the 1975 original it's not as good, but I now feel Black Christmas (2006) is still a pretty decent slasher film that stands well enough on it's own &amp; deserves more recognition than it has been getting since it's release. The film is certainly well acted, with each of the girls putting in a really good performance &amp; best of all they're all gorgeous too! The direction by JAMES WONG is expertly done, as he is able to conjure up a sense of mood &amp; creepiness to the proceedings. Since this is an updated for the times remake, Black Christmas (2006) also happens to have a much higher body count &amp; tends to be a lot more bloody &amp; violent, not to mention over the top in the executions of the kills, apart from the original film, who's deaths were mostly kept off screen. Here the kills are decidedly nasty &amp; all have a weird Christmas theme to them: We get a Christmas ornament to the eye, an icicle to the eye, pulled out eyeballs, a sharp candy cane to the neck, a vicious beheading, strangulation with Christmas lights, a tree decorated with human eyeballs &amp; a severed head, a vicious beating with a roller pin, flesh carved away from a body &amp; turned into Christmas cookies &amp; in an even grosser twist, a couple of the victims are cannibalized, the back of a skull is hacked off with an ice skate, we get a garden trowel to the face &amp; in a tribute to the original films most infamous kill, a victim is smothered via a plastic bag that is placed over her head, before getting a knife plunged into it to stop her from moving, ultimately though, unlike the 1975 film, it doesn't spend to much time with this corpse, as it is only seen for a couple frames in the movie &amp; the glass unicorn death scene is also done again, only extra bloody &amp; these are just some of the methods of death employed. The film also displays a few nude bodies &amp; a few sexual elements, one which disturbingly involves incest. Also grafted onto the film is a back story for the killer Billy &amp; his unseen (in the original) sister Agnes, detailing their somewhat sick &amp; twisted past. To be truthful, the film really takes very little from the original movie, who's story was set over a series of a few days leading up to Christmas eve. Black Christmas 06' story is set entirely over one night &amp; discards the father looking for his missing daughter subplot, to an extent, replacing the dad with an older sister, who has come looking for her sibling when she fails to show up. It also discards the police officer character played by JOHN SAXON in the first &amp; the subplot involving one of the girls being pregnant &amp; considering an abortion &amp; the boyfriend who may or may not be doing the killings &amp; in a nice nod to the original film, Billy escapes from the "Clark Sanitarium" which is a nod to the original films director, the late BOB CLARK &amp; ANDREA MARTIN being cast in the role of the house mother after playing one of the sorority girls in the 1975 film was a nice touch (yet somehow I can't help but feel that the film was just begging for MARGOT KIDDER to take the role &amp; have made it much more fun!) the film tends to use the holiday setting &amp; integrate it better into it's story &amp; setting, than the first one did, as there is plenty of Christmas sites &amp; themes abounding &amp; Wong &amp; company are able to deliver a nice polished &amp; sleek look to the proceedings, ditching the darker, greener, grainier look of the 75' version &amp; I felt adding a subplot surrounding the relationship between sorority girl Kelly &amp; Lea, one of the older sisters of the sorority girls, was a nice touch &amp; the film even goes in depth on the history of Christmas, during a conversation between the girls, where one of them let's the others in on the fact that Christmas originates with pagan &amp; not Christian religion.On the downside however, perhaps Black Christmas 06's greatest down fall is that it tends at times to not know when to quit. The film is really good, tight &amp; suspenseful &amp; is a lot of fun to watch for horror fans, but the film-makers seem to drop the ball in the last fifteen minutes when the film falls apart with a somewhat okay, but ludicrous ending, that felt out of place on the film &amp; the film tends to sacrifice a lot of the suspense of the first for more stylish out &amp; out gore &amp; the back story involving Billy &amp; how his sister really came to be, comes off as a little to trashy at times to the point where one could almost consider it instant sleaze.Apart from that, Black Christmas 06' is a nice edition to any slasher fans horror movie library &amp; works well enough to stand on it's own, as a nice bloody slasher gem. See it!***1/2 stars</fullReview>
	</review>

		<shortDescription>God Awful! I mean BAD and I'm a lenient reviewer!</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>This film gets a special 2/10 grade from me because there is one redeeming factor in this film. The girls are very hot. There is no doubt about it that Katie Cassidy, Michelle Trachtenberg, Lacey Chabert, Mary Elizabeth Winstead, and Crystal Lowe are incredibly gorgeous. Their looks keep you glued to the screen during this god awful remake to, one of my favorite horror films, Black Christmas. Too bad their beauty can't save the film from being by far the most awful film of 2006. Maybe I'm being bitter because I love the original so much but the filmmakers should be ashamed of themselves for butchering the originals good name.I'd like to point out that earlier this year director Glen Morgan talked very angrily about the When A Stranger Calls remake. He said that he had saw the film and that Black Christmas would not go down the same path as that film. He said that the film was sub-par and that Black Christmas would be much better. Well, Mr. Morgan I'm going to say that the mediocre mess known as When A Stranger Calls is hands down a much better film than your take on Black Christmas. I have to ask myself has this guy even seen the original film? Did he simply think it had a cool title and just wanted to make his own story and sell it as a remake? To fans of the original there are no similarities except that it takes place on Christmas, it involves someone named Billy, and there are sorority girls. Other than that this film is much different and definitely not in a better way.The first major mistake is providing a backstory for "Billy". The original film allowed us to imagine what might have drove Billy to the point of murdering the sorority girls. The fact that we learned very little about him or even saw what he looked like, added to the overall mystery of the character. In the 2006 version, we get so much backstory that it truly makes him a rather neutered villain. They go down the typical he went crazy and killed his family route which resulted in him being locked up in a sanitarium. Of course on Christmas Eve he breaks out and decides to stalk the sorority house which turns out to be his former home. There is no mystery and no intrigue whatsoever. It also doesn't help that the flashback scenes of Billy's childhood are so sloppily handled that they actually slip into unintentional comedy. I literally laughed out loud due to some of the absurdity of these scenes. They don't mesh well with the already horrendously bad present day story.Then there are the sorority girls. Not one of them is likable. Even the heroine is a bit annoying and she definitely doesn't have the same virtue as the Olivia Hussey character from the original film. It seems like, with the exception of Katie Cassidy and Mary Elizabeth Winstead, that everyone is running on auto bitch pilot. They are nasty, evil, and just plain superficial. If you were to ask me the difference between the Michelle Trachtenberg character and the Lacey Chabert character, I really couldn't tell you. For some reason the screenwriter wanted all the female characters to be exactly alike which gives the audience no one to root for. In fact, I couldn't wait for most of them to meet their demise.The film is also excessively gory. Some might call this a blessing but in the case of this film, it is a major roadblock. The original film had little to no blood in it but of course in today's horror movie market you have to gross out the audience, so Black Christmas does just that. The problem is the violence isn't visceral, it appears to be purely comical. I didn't turn away once out of fright but I certainly laughed at how ridiculous the violence was. I shouldn't be laughing at a killer eating human eye balls but Black Christmas makes you do just that. The film leaves very little to the imagination and positively kills one of the best aspects of the original film.The acting is a non-issue. No one here is any good. I've seen many of these actresses do very well in other projects but Black Christmas should be removed from their resumes if they hope to gain respect in the industry. They are all beautiful girls (I for one am surprised by how grown up Michelle Trachtenberg and Lacey Chabert look in the film) but beauty can only get you so far. They all scream well but the script and the film does nothing for them. They all leave the film looking a little embarrassed with themselves.The only thing I hope this film does is allow audiences to discover the original film. I implore you people discover the 1974 classic and please ignore the 2006 remake. It is a disgrace and I hope it dies a quick death never to be heard from again. Do yourself a favor and avoid this trainwreck at all cost but feel free to buy the new special edition of the original film which is currently found in stores. This new version is definitely one to miss unless you need a good laugh.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Should be called "The People in the Walls"</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Since this is a remake you can't help comparing it to the original. Black Christmas (1974) was a first-rate horror thriller that paved the way for horror films to come. It's been imitated a lot over the years so maybe it was inevitable that a remake would surface. While the original is best known for it's tremendously scary atmosphere and gruelling tension this remake goes in another direction entirely. It's brutal, gory and very fast paced. None of it good, by the way.In the original viewers were left to fill in the blanks concerning Billy. What were his motives? What was his background? Who the hell was Agnes? And more. Here everything is explained away and I don't think I'm the only one who considers this script not even worthy of wiping somebody's ass. I won't spoil anything but here you'll find out Billy's reasons for his homicidal spree and you also get the lowdown on Agnes.If we leave the technical aspects of this film aside, there's one thing severely lacking here: TALENT. The director is also credited for the script so we can put most of the blame on him. There's no tension to be found, any attempt at creating a creepy atmosphere is laughable and the characters are not only annoying but very badly acted. But to their credit, their roles were beyond bad anyway.The film just jumps from one kill to the next and a great effort is put into making things very gross (such as Billy's eating preference etc.). It's O.K. to make the kills somewhat brutal, but that seems to be the only thing that's accomplished with any skill. The dialogue here is horrible and I guess the director thought it was hip and cool to have everybody hating Christmas and poor old Santa takes a beating this time around, being called a perv and also of course he's referred to as Santa "f******" Claus. The whole script looks like it was written by a teenager.As said, the kills are brutal and not completely without imagination but that simply doesn't count for much when the film is devoid of suspense and no tension at all. It's very predictable as well. Overall I'd say it's offensive to remake a classic horror film in this way. One can only wonder as to how bad a script has to be to get the axe.The two stars go to the technical department who have done a good job. The lighting schemes are on occasion great and the kills are done in a splendid way.Final verdict: Very bad film and not even of interest to genre fans.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>What Makes this a remake?</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>When it comes to remakes, there are two types of directions one can take.The first, a scene for scene remake, has become redundant. Psycho didn't work as a remake.The second can sometimes work: in my opinion it worked quite well for the 2006 remake of The Hills Have Eyes." Black Christmas finds itself decidedly in this second category.For those who are interested, the original film was about a disturbed and unknown killer who stalks the girls of a sorority and one by one picks them off, making an obligatory and frightening phone call in the short time after their death.In the remake, the spirit of this is there: the phone calls usually (but not always) come after a murder, there is a disturbed pair (no one killer here) stalking the girls, and...well, that is where the similarities end. Unless you count Andrea Martin being in both of them (an ironic twist for those of us who remember how sweet, pragmatic and young she was when the original was made), or the first victim being named "Clair." This film is a mess. Unlike the original, where Billy was a personality on the phone who seemed to have a malevolence...and was only exposed as the killer at the end, we know that "Billy" is the killer all through this film. We know Billy's story- this in itself works against the film because a lot of the mystery of the original came from the possibility that one of the guys (most likely Peter, in the original) was capable of resembling a normal guy on the outside, but being so vicious and demented on the inside that he was capable of vicious acts of evil.Billy was born with yellow skin, and was loved by his father and hated by his mother. One Christmas as a young boy he finds a present to him from "Santa," hears his parents arguing, and ventures downstairs to witness his father viciously murdered by his mother and her companion in adultery. It is at this point that Billy is locked in the attic.Over the next few years, Billy is "blessed" with a new sister/daughter (this has to be seen to be believed), kills his mother and stepfather, and eats the eyeball (a recurring theme in this movie) of his daughter/sister before he munches down some Christmas cookies made from the flesh of his dead mother.He's institutionalized, hatches a plan to escape, and reunites with his daughter/sister who has become as demented as he is, and who has started to murder the girls at the sorority.This film doesn't excel in any area: its not smart enough to be effective, not gory enough to be disgusting, and not well acted enough to be effective. Among some of the most obvious gaffes...before she dies, Clair starts a card for her sister's gift with "Leigh," - however when Leigh in fact finds the gift, it reads "To my big sister Leigh; from your baby sister Clair." I think the biggest load of all however is the pair of killers. Billy isn't so much a problem...but his sister/daughter is so obviously a man that all throughout the film, I couldn't help but think of the WWE wrestler Kane in a blonde wig... I wonder where he was when this film was being shot??? The film does have some very minor bright spots: Andrea Martin's presence in it; a rather post modernist interpretation of Christmas and so on...however this film really has nothing worth watching! Its really disappointing that in a film that was so effective in 1974 that its still scary in 2006, they had to remake such a film into THIS!</fullReview>

		<fullReview>Have mixed feelings about this remake. It had all the potential to be a good, solid, suspenseful horror/thriller, but director Glen Morgan apparently decided that instead of trying to scare the audience, it would be far easier and simpler to gross them out. As a lifelong horror/slasher movie fan, I don't consider myself squeamish, and I've happily sat through gorier films than this, but there are some surprisingly gruesome scenes. I'm amazed that Black Christmas 2006 only received a 15 certificate here in the UK - what does a film have to do to get an 18 these days? The most depressing thing about the gore in this film is that it's so calculated. As I've stated above, Morgan has just gone straight for the audience's stomachs, rather than their nerve endings (it reminded me of all those slasher movies that followed in Halloween's wake in the early Eighties, made by directors who lacked John Carpenter's talent, so they threw blood and guts at the camera to compensate). Presumably Morgan, the producers, and/or the studio felt that recent films such as Hostal and the Saw series have raised the bar regarding cinematic bloodletting, and they had to do the same to compete.The phone calls that were such a key element of the original Black Christmas are still included in this remake, but there're not an important part of the story. I suspect they've been de-emphasised to avoid comparisons with the When A Stranger Calls remake that was released earlier in 2006 (which is ironic, seeing as how the original When A Stranger Calls - released in 1979 - owed a clear debt to the original Black Christmas - released in 1974). Instead, a new element is introduced: a series of flashbacks that reveal the Jerry-Springer-on-acid life story of the film's psycho villain, but these are mostly unnecessary, add nothing to the narrative other than slow it down, and don't succeed in making the killer a more interesting or threatening figure. Their inclusion appears to be solely to add to the yuck factor. It would have been more effective to simply have the killer's history revealed in a monologue delivered by another character.Yet another disappointment is the fact that having gathered together a great, once-in-a lifetime cast of up-and-coming young starlets, the script gives them so little to do, other than react to events. Most of the characters are barely two-dimensional and completely interchangeable, and if you wanted to be cynical, you could suspect that the main reason the producers cast so many familiar faces was simply to help the audience tell the characters apart.Some of the other casting decisions are bizarre. A character who appears in a '15 years ago' flashback is played by the same actor in present-day scenes, but no attempt seems to have been made to make him look as though he's aged at all. The grown-up child of another character is played by someone who actually looks older than the actor portraying the parent! And if that wasn't enough, one key character is played by an actor of the opposite gender - and it shows.Ultimately what little goodwill the movie does generate is mostly ruined by the rushed, clichéd and logic-free ending. Although much inferior to the classic original, Black Christmas 2006 isn't truly a bad film - if it was, I would easily dismiss it as such. Instead it's that perhaps even more frustrating animal, a movie that had all the necessary ingredients and could have been really good - but fell short and ended up as merely being adequate.But what do I know? The audience I saw the film with (the majority of whom were younger than me) all screamed, giggled, gasped and yelled "eeow!" at the appropriate moments. I suspect most of them were texting their mates about the movie as they left the cinema.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<shortDescription>A Great Slasher!</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>This film is probably the best horror film I've seen in the past two years and the best slasher film (for me anyway) since I Know What You Did Last Summer. Now don't get me wrong, plot holes and character stupidity are all present throughout the film but the film succeeds in one major aspect that so many other horror films fail miserably at: its characters.Every single one of the characters I cared about. When each met their demise, I was truly sad except one of the characters who was pretty creepy and suspicious for the two minutes they were actually in. But getting back to the point, this was the film's major redeeming factor along with the death scenes (which are over-the-top and gory).Knowing that each character wasn't really based on a stereotype made me forgive their stupid mistakes (like going out alone to turn the power back on, etc). For the most part, this slasher film is a fun 'slay' ride. It doesn't hold a candle to the original for the fans but even though I liked the first one, the remake is the movie I'd prefer to watch. While the first one was great, it did get a little slow in the middle.One major disappointment I do need to point out though is that Billy was not creepy enough. He seemed a looked a little too normal to be as frightening as Jason Voorhees or Michael Myers.Anyway, this is one of the few horror remakes that is actually decent (another good remake of recent times is House of Wax). I'd recommend this film to slasher/horror movie fans but if you don't like the genre, this isn't going to change your views on it.</fullReview>

		<date>2013-12-09</date>
		<username>bayardhiler</username>
		<score>0.1</score>
		<shortDescription>A Christmas Slasher Remake? Bah Humbug!!!!</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Usually Christmas is a time of happiness, family, presents, Christmas trees, lights, decorations, and any and all other Christmas cheer. But for some people, Christmas time is merely another way to think up a plot to another slasher film, like this trainwreck of a movie, 2006's version of "Black Christmas". Before I go any further, let me say that I have seen the original 1974 version of "Black Christmas" and while I can't say it was the greatest horror film I ever saw, at least it was better than this. This "update" follows the same basic plot of the original, in which a group of sorority girls were being stalked and killed one by one in their creepy sorority house by a mysterious, unseen killer. But the "update", in an attempt to be different from the original, fails to incorporate the things that made the original decent. Firstly, they reveal the identity of the killer almost right from the beginning as a disturbed man named Billy who grew up and was abused by his mother in the house that now houses the sorority. For whatever reason, the writers here decide to have Billy diagnosed with liver disease, which causes his skin to turn a comical bright yellow. Now it is true that people who have liver disease can indeed have yellow skin; however, it's a slight tint of yellow. Here, the skin of the character is so bright yellow that he looks like a live character from "The Simpsons"!In Bob Clark's '74 version, we never knew who the killer was since we only saw thing from his point of view or if we were lucky his shadow and occasional eyeball, thus making the film all the more spooky. But here, not only do they reveal the killer, they also feel the need to throw in an unnecessary back story involving incest and cannibalism that was probably intended to shock but instead merely disgusts. As for the victims, due to the lack of character development they come across as no more than cannon fodder so the producers can skip setting up mood and atmosphere and get right to the gore. The characters are so bland and interchangeable that we don't even know half their names or even care whether they live or die. At least in the '74 version, we kind of cared and felt for the ladies in distress. The writing is so devoid of logic that I can't even write too many examples without laughing hysterically. I'll just say this: if you're in a dark house and several of your friends go missing and you start receiving creepy messages sent by their phones, would you stay in that house???!!! Oh and as for the big twist that the producers promised in the DVD extra, it's so flat and unimpressive that it really makes no difference to the overall film. The result of all this is a pointless film that lacks tension, spookiness, and good storytelling. So to sum it all up, if you are someone who feels the need to spend Christmas watching young woman being stalked and murdered by a sadistic killer (hey, it's the holiday season!) then at the very least, I recommend that you stick to the original Bob Clark version. Merry Christmas and a Happy New Year, if one can say that at the end of this film!</fullReview>
	</review>

		<username>Chris Smith (RockPortReview)</username>
		<score>0.5</score>
		<shortDescription>A Decent remake, but still not as good as the original</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>The recent trend of remaking classic horror movies is hopefully on the decline, but not without leaving several horrible films in its wake. Very few ever come close the original but with "Black Christmas" in 2007 the filmmakers did a good enough job not to embarrass themselves, and actually make a decent movie.Taking place within a sorority house the day before Christmas break a group of girls and their house mother are terrorized by a former inhabitant named Billy Lenz. Billy has quite the back story and its told in flashbacks throughout the movie. Its extremely disturbing and involves murder, incest, and all those beloved family pastimes. Born with yellow skin and rejected by his psychotic mother, Billy lives most of his life locked in the attic. As a teenager Billy is raped by his mother and she has a baby girl. When he finally gets out he kills his mother and makes Christmas cookies out of her skin (Yummy!!). His sister disappears and Billy is caught and sent to a mental hospital. Years later he escapes (naturally) and heads back home to the now sorority house.The girls start receiving prank calls and one by one they start to disappear. The story had been modernized from the original 1974 version. Cell phones play a big part, as well as computers. Although the characters and killings do bear some resemblance to the original. Like a lot or horror remakes this is more of a re-imagining of the story rather that a shot for shot remake. A lot of horror clichés are used but are used effectively. The girls are pretty one dimensional and serve as victims quite well. There is a big shock ending that makes you sort of rethink a lot of what you just saw. Paying close attention to the flashbacks should help. Unlike a lot of the recent remakes which water down the violence and gore to get a PG-13 rating "Black Christmas" takes pleasure in making it R rated with gruesome kills and gory pieces all over. The DVD includes a "making of" and Director's notebook features and is definitely worth a buy. You can find used copies for very cheap all over the internet. The original 1974 film is also available on DVD and blu-ray and is essential viewing for all horror fans.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Tales From The Horror Genre #2</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>I feel almost bad about not giving this film a favorable review?almost. I have these feelings because, when the lead characters begin to die, "Black Christmas" becomes a relatively effective slasher flick. Unfortunately, that comes all too late and lasts for only a short time, with most of the characters being killed off in a twenty minute interval. Certainly, when they do die, they die with enough sprayed blood and creativity to make even the most jaded gore-hound wince, but that cannot make up for the fact that the rest of this film's runtime is dedicated to some of the worst flashbacks in recent memory and a lot of under-developed drama between our soon-to-be victims, as well as a lifeless whodunit that is never entertaining or compelling. The remake of a rather ingenuous little slasher flick of the same name, "Black Christmas" had a large legacy to live up to and, though it might be passable to some, it stumbles in its forefather's shadow.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Black X-Mas, BESTWORST</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>There are bad movies, and then there is "Black Christmas," or as the DVD box calls it, "Black Xmas" (undoubtedly a reference to E.E. Cummings). Black Christmas isn't just bad, it's awful and shocking in a manner that I usually expect only from new Black Eyed Peas singles. "Black Christmas" is the Olympics of bad. It's the 8th wonder of the world bad. It's Uwe Boll bad.Black Christmas tells the story of a creepy guy killing various nubile femmes during a snowy evening. Many people die from falling objects, including an icicle, from 4 feet overhead. Then, they throw a flaming Christmas tree through a wall.It's a coat hanger abortion of a movie that is too standard to interest the hardcore genre fans and too grisly to work for the casual viewer. Every decision is wrong. Every moment forced. Yes, there is a plethora of attractive female leads, but a good horror film this does not make.Fortunately, black Christmas is bad in the way that few films are. It's mesmerizing bad. It's hilariously bad. It's the kind of movie you realize is stupid, even when you're watching it stoned, which is the only way I can really recommend anyone watching it, (I was sober by the way). And that's its biggest strength. The movie is drenched in a kind of morbid, "how bad can this possibly get" type vibe.From the girl with the 6 inch thick glasses that make her face look like an anime character to the reveal of the killer, to the flaming Christmas tree thrown inside of a wall, everything in this movie is insane. The filmmakers looked at Christmas and tried to think of every single imaginable way to deface the holiday. As an agnostic male of Jewish descent, I found this terribly amusing. Unfortunately, it's done with all the panache of a 9-year old just learning swear words and so, it's markedly less effective than say, "Bad Santa" after which "Black Christmas" seems to be modeled.But, unlike Billy Bob Thornton's curmudgeonly Magnum Opus , Black Christmas never generates any warmth from it's black coal of a heart and so the whole affair ends up as lifeless as the various corpses strewn across the screen.The film is a remake of Bob Clark's second most frightening film (behind Baby Geniuses 2: Super Babies) but it basically ignores everything that film had to offer. I haven't seen it in years, but I don't recall the method of killing, the motivation or the ending being even vaguely similar. There is the clear plastic suffocation thing going on still and the Christmas setting, but otherwise, this film totally abandons everything cool about the original, including the ambiguous ending.There are a few nice camera angles, but overall this movie feels like amateur hour. Written and directed by Glen Morgan, (sans his usual partner James Wong), before being forced into massive reshoots just weeks before its release, Black Christmas hits only sour notes. But it does so in a sort of compelling way.</fullReview>

Billy escapes from his prison/institution in the most unlikely circumstances and is ready to go back and pick of where he left. Everything is predictable and again you have a story that develops only because everybody acts in a totally retarded way. I will not even bother to describe the flaws in this movie. It reminded me to a certain point of Carpenters "Halloween" but lacks the acting of a Donald Pleasence and Jamie Lee Curtis.If you want cinematic junk food watch this movie. Just remember that you will never get those 80 minutes back again./Simon</fullReview>

		<username>dav07dan02</username>
		<score>0.6</score>
		<shortDescription>clark institution</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Director/Script:Glen Morgan (Based on the 1974 screenplay by Roy More), Cast: Katie Cassidy (Kelli), Michelle Trachtenberg (Melisa), Mary Elizabeth Winstead (Heather), Lacey Chabert (Dana), Kristen Cloke (Leigh), Andrea Martin (Ms. Mac), Crystal Lowe (Lauren), Oliver Hudson (Kyle), Kathleen Kole (Eve).I think that people's opinion of this movie is going to be largely divided. There will be many young people (who perhaps are not familiar with the original film) that think it is absolutely great and of course many fans of the original that will think it 'sucks'. When I review a remake, I try to do so with and open mind and not always compare it with the original film. I am certainly guilty of this! One thing many fans of the original can agree on regardless of their opinion of this film is that it will certainly bring a lot of attention to the obscure original. Then again, us horror fanatics (like myself!) get a little possessive of our movies. We don't want them to appeal to the masses. So who knows.This is the second remake attempt by director Glen Morgan. The other was Willard. I thought Willard was a good film, perhaps better than the original.His second remake attempt was of course,Black Christmas. It is a totally different script and with just a couple of exceptions has different characters. The similarities are of course the title, the concept of the sorority house, and the 'Billy' and 'Agnus' characters. In the first film, we never really get to know who the killer is. Who 'Billy' was is left a mystery. I think this is what made the first film such a classic. Much of the first half of this film is devoted to telling the story of 'Billy' and 'Agnus'. We are told about Billy's background and what led him to kill. We also find out who Agnus is. As it turns out, the sorority house was Billy's childhood home and a lot of bad things happened to him there! Most of the murder and mayhem occurs during the second half of the film. Morgan uses a lot of fast passed action to move the film along which builds to a climatic ending. The first film was much more plot and character driven whereas this uses more visuals. Also, we see a lot more graphic violence in this one. Eye balls gouged out (and eaten!), severed heads etc. I actually find the over the top gore to be rather tongue-and cheek. Being a huge fan of the original, I had long anticipated seeing this film. Overall all, I was not disappointed. I appreciate the fact that they did not just rehash the original script. I think they did a good job telling the story of Billy. The films biggest weakness was the lack of character development and personality in the characters. I find this a problem in many of today's films. All the actors seems the same! You will not see anybody with the class of Oliva Hussey, the sarcastic wit of Margot Kidder or cool like John Saxon. Although I was glad to see Andria Martin from the original in this film, I wish they would have given her a different part. I kind off wish they would have made her character more like the house mother in the original. She is a comedian as well as an actress. I think they made her too serious. See for yourself if he did justice to Bob Clark's original. I knew I wouldn't be able to do this review without comparing it to the original!</fullReview>
	</review>

		<username>Robert W. (Robert_duder@hotmail.com)</username>
		<score>0.5</score>
		<shortDescription>Kind of a dud, a rushed remake but it's good for some laughs</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Black Christmas is nothing to write home about. I think I have seen the original cult classic but it has been absolutely years so I was kind of looking forward to checking out this remake in hopes it might have some decent surprises. I won't crap too much on this film because I didn't feel like I wasted any time watching it. For what it was worth it was decently entertaining slasher gore flick with no real purpose or story other than to have a killer stalk a sorority house and despite their attempts to give the story some depth it never really works. Even with some decent performances on the part of the main cast, it wasn't written well enough to do much of anything. It's a forgettable but at least watchable campy, horror flick. Director Glen Morgan is quite new to direction, his previous film being Willard which also tanked (I have yet to see it), but this is still no excuse for Mr. Morgan as he has produced and written for some much better films including Final Destination one and three and several episodes of The X-Files. Granted the budget of Black Christmas was quite small although still nearly twenty times what the budget of the original film was.Katie Cassidy plays the as close to the lead girl in the film as the film has. She's the main scream queen so to speak. She does a decent job of running around the house scared for her life but nothing outstanding. She isn't given an incredible script to work with. Michelle Trachtenberg who I do think is a gifted actor in such roles as Buffy The Vampire Slayer, House, and Ice Princess is barely alert as the snotty and annoyed Melissa Kitt. Kristen Cloke, Crystal Lowe, Lacey Chabert (also a decent actress), and Mary Elizabeth Winstead are the rest of the sorority victims and other than being this they serve little purpose to any plot or reason to the film. Besides a light story surrounding the main girl (Cassidy) there is hardly any character development other than watching the girls get taken, phone call to the house, and then murdered in some twisted way. One brighter spot to the film is the performance by Oliver Hudson who plays Cassidy's estranged boyfriend. He is a stronger player and has more personality in general and is more watchable. Since he's dating the main character he is almost certain to live. Veteran Canadian comedienne Andrea Martin plays the Sorority house mother and just seems vapid and annoying with no real purpose.So after covering all this how can I say the film is watchable?? Well from a horror fan perspective there is plenty of death scenes and plenty of blood and the phone calls are a nice touch, if not entirely unoriginal. The hoarse whisper of "They're my family now" adds a certain aspect to the creepy factor. And I give them props for attempting a decent back story on the killer and his sister and opening the film up for plenty of bad sequels which I am all for when it comes to Horror films. Black Christmas might even make you jump but it's predictable, rehashed and slapped together in every sense of the word. True Horror fans might get a kick out of it but everyone else will likely hate it and find it a waste of time. 5/10</fullReview>

What would be better than taking an already created movie, adding some new effects (thanks to modern technology), manipulating the plot or adding subplots (ideas that are rarely good) and in horror movies specifically, adding more screams and gore, which is exactly the case with Black Christmas. I mean, this movie set standards for later films like Halloween and Friday the 13th. The killings were few, but the film was still eerie and scary. As for the remake, I would describe it in one word "LAME". It has too many killings. The main plot is fragile (can anyone believe you can escape a sanitarium that easily?). 		<date>2006-12-26</date>
		<username>jockk407</username>
		<score>0.3</score>
		<shortDescription>A Yuletide Dud</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>With the recent glut of remakes being vomited up by Hollyworthless, horror fans over the age of 25 don't have much original to look forward to, and for every good remake like THE HILLS HAVE EYES there are three duds (the atrocious THE FOG, the worthless AMITYVILLE HORROR, the juvenile WHEN A STRANGER CALLS). Sadly, BLACK Christmas, while not as bad as any of those remakes, must fall into the same category. Hopefully Bob Clark was well-paid.Horror fans who haven't seen the original (and if you are a horror fan and haven't, shame on you) will probably enjoy this a little more than those familiar with the 1974 classic, but most will agree it's nothing more than an episodic mess of clichés and missed-opportunities. The situations are preposterous, the murders are gory but repetitive and unexciting, and director Morgan tries to keep the pace so rapid he doesn't develop any sense of dread or suspense until the last 20 minutes or so, and by then it's too late. A very well done set-piece involving a girl stuck behind a wall manages to escalate quite well, showing that Morgan, who did so well with the original FINAL DESTINATION and the underrated WILLARD, can still film a payoff.But that's the heart of the problem with this film, it's all pay-off and no build-up. The actresses are all completely interchangeable: pretty, vapid, bitchy, and unable to deliver the acerbic dialogue with even the slightest hint of believability. One actress (doesn't matter which one, I couldn't tell them apart) delivers a speech about the true origin of Christmas that is supposed to be a witty and shocking centerpiece to the film, but spurts it out with such precision it's as if she memorized it word for word using flash cards just hours before. Even gifted comedian Andrea Martin, who played one of the main girls in the original and here takes over the role of house-mother, seems to be sleepwalking, which is just as well, since a role that was so juicy in the first film is underwritten into obscurity here.There are moments when the film springs to life. I liked some of the attention to detail in the beginning, I loved how they updated the obscene phone calls to incorporate cell phones, the Christmas atmosphere is well-photographed, and Billy's back story is surprisingly well-handled. But everything plugs along at a can't-hardly-wait pace, killing the mood and suspense. The director also uses funky angles, fish-eye lenses, and dangling cameras to try and create a feeling of unease. But this backfires, since there is no narrative drive to connect with, and no time to care. I felt more sympathy for Billy in the early scenes than anyone else in the film.BLACK Christmas can at least be credited for one thing: Many groups have attacked the film for being in spectacularly bad taste (all the Christmas bashing, child abuse, even incest), and for once they are correct. It IS in bad taste, and that's one of its few charms, and one of the few things that work. It's often unpleasant, sure, but it goes for it and doesn't shy away...this is pitch black humor with no tongue-in-cheek.But finally in the end it's just a below average slasher film with big studio production values. Someone somewhere in those big studios is still convinced you have to have a killing, a jump, or a loud noise at least once every five minutes to keep an audience's attention.I'll bet it won't even take that long to forget the entire film.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<username>aimless-46</username>
		<score>0.2</score>
		<shortDescription>About As Bad As It Can Get</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>You have to make certain allowances for the familial horror genre and the sorority house sub-genre, as their target audiences do not place a premium on intelligent scripting, even the few of them who actually have the capacity to appreciate it. Yet even by the low brain wattage standards of its genre, "Black Xmas" (2006) ranks pretty near the bottom. It you are looking for self-parody elements the pickings are very slim. The only good one is what the production designers did in setting up the 1991 flashback scene of the kitchen. Instead of a 1991 kitchen they give you a 1948ish "Christmas Story" kitchen complete with a returnable glass milk bottle, a self-reflexive reference to that film's director Bob Clark, who also directed the original "Black Christmas" (1974). More obvious is having Michelle Trachtenberg's character impaled on an ice skate blade (insert "Ice Princess" 2005 here). It used to be that even when this type of film failed on multiple levels: stupid plot (insert talent challenged here), impossibly contrived story (insert lazy here), implausibly indestructible and all-knowing villain (insert lazy again), bad acting and directing (insert talent challenged again), shoddy editing (insert damage control here); it still managed to be a least somewhat creepy. Even something as awful as "Cabin Fever" managed that (although I'm still not sure how). And even the worst of the horror parodies and el-cheapo exploitation efforts contained enough hot babes in sexy situations that there was some reason to watch the screen. This might be the most puzzling element about "Black Xmas", simply because it would have been so easy to include it. Why would you make the setting a sorority house and then ignore the opportunity to insert those elements? Good grief the director had both Trachtenberg and Mary Elizabeth Winstead in the cast; two of the hottest looking actresses in Hollywood. Yet they are only shown in wide master shots with lighting as dim as the scriptwriter's brain activity level. In fact the only genuinely homely actress (Crystal Lowe-whose face looks strangely rearranged and who really should avoid scenes with someone who looks like Trachtenberg) in the entire cast gets all the well- lighted close-ups (insert the sound of gagging here). And they wonder why these things lose money. I'll also point out a major violation of the principles governing the language of film. I don't know if this was ignorance, stupidity, or accident but an error this basic causes a viewer to have total contempt for the production. The film opens with two murders in the sorority house and yet you see that Billy Lentz (the villain) is still locked up in the hospital. Then we get a flashback to the 1975 conception of Billy's sister. They go out of the flashback with a shot of the baby sister, to a match cut close-up of Eve, the somewhat odd (creepy??) sorority sister (although even in nerd glasses she is yet another actress Lowe should stay away from). In film an edit like this is supposed to communicate (director to viewer) a subtle (but always truthful) clue that Eve is Billy's sister; so later you look back and see that the clue was there to see that Eve had committed the murders that occurred prior to Billy's escape. It would have been a terrific cut and at the time it really raised my expectations the film would be working on multiple levels. Unfortunately Eve is killed almost immediately after, which tends to support the theory that the edit occurred entirely by accident. Speaking of editing, one thing that made the original so effective was the subtle juxtapositions of violence and gore with gently twinkling Christmas lights, songs, traditions, and a feeling or warmth. The remake attempts to capture this same thing but the images are so contrived (both the violence and the decorations) that you never buy into either and even if their was effective editing (there isn't) it could not save the day. As bogus as the production is, the most glaring scenes are those that might be considered under the classification of drama. The romance and the sudden appearance of an older sister come to mind as some of the worst acted sequences you are likely to find in any mainstream production. And of course the completely unnecessary insertion of an older actress only takes away from the screen time of the already underutilized "attractive" actresses. What was that about wondering why these things lose money? Toward the end the story has to throw out any remaining credibility and ask that you suspend all disbelief and believe that the extremely low-budget storm outside has caused cross-town rescuers a two-hour delay when the characters have been coming and going without incident up until that moment. Then again, what do I know? I'm only a child.</fullReview>

Back in 1970 a boy by the name of Billy lived there. His alcoholic mother hated him because he looked so much like his father (who was actually a nice guy). The mother finds herself a new man and has to off the father. Little Billy sees this so the mother locks him up in the attic and subjects him to a life of abuse. Don't fall asleep, there is more to this story. Flash forward to 1982 and we see the mother enjoying life with her new man. Well being that the new guy is a drunk too he can never seem to finish the deed when they are having sex. What's a girl to do? Solution! Go up to the attic and rape your son. She then becomes pregnant with her son's child. Nine months later she gives birth to a girl named Agnes. Flash forward to 1991. Now this movie has a few pathetic twists and turns so even though Billy is set up as the lead killer it becomes quite clear that he is not the only one responsible for the carnage. This leads to an annoying parade of suspects who just show up inexplicably out of nowhere.This movie should have been called 'The Dummies Guide To Clichés' since it uses EVERY SINGLE ONE KNOW TO MAN. Wait, I take that back! It did not contain a cat popping out scene and that is probably it's most creative surprise. There are no good scares and I sat very still in my chair during all of the scenes that were intended to make the audience jump. Not good.This film does not follow the same path of the original by crafting a suspenseful and creepy tale. Instead it chooses to go down the gore route. So how does the gore fair? Not very impressive in the first hour (the camera cuts away too soon during the kills and/or we just get the same old tired ass shot of blood spraying against the wall. YAWN.) However it does get much better in the last half hour. There is one actual 'DAYUM!!!!' death scene and some very cool yet not very Martha Stewart like Christmas decorations.The only other nice thing I can say about 'Black Christmas(2006)' is that the filmmakers gorgeous use of colors and lighting translate into some big screen eye candy. On the other side of the coin, it works against the film too. It almost looks as though they were trying to make a Tim Burton version of a slasher movie. And unlike chocolate and peanut butter that is not a combination that goes well together.So what can else can I say? This film is a mess from start to finish. My advice would be to avoid it. Avoid it like you avoided that Carmen Electra/Dave Navarro reality T.V. show</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Should Satisfy Slasher Fans</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>While this film is no classic, and certainly doesn't come close to matching the original, it should satisfy its audience -- those craving lurid, gruesome shocks amid the otherwise feel-good fare playing during Christmas.From the start, the film abandons its predecessor's subtle, suspenseful approach to the story of a maniac preying on unsuspecting sorority sisters. Instead, the makers of this film dump loads of gore on the story. Actually, after this year's anemic, highly predictable When a Stranger Calls, I was relieved that this film's makers --perhaps sensing that the hoary premise itself, saddled with the usual slasher clichés, couldn't stand alone on its own merits -- saturated the film in deliciously outrageous blood-and-guts gore. Alas, some of the kills aren't as gory as I was expecting, based on what I had read on the Internet, but they nevertheless should satisfy the gore connoisseur.Perhaps the best parts of the film are scenes depicting Billy's back story. These scenes, packed with the debauched details of abuse by Billy's monstrous mother, appear in patches throughout the film whenever the present narrative threatens to become too boring and predictable.Also on display are steaming HOT chicks lined up for slaughter. The actress playing Lacey and actress Michelle T. (of Buffy fame) are particularly striking presentations of female pulchritude. Alas, the nudity, unlike the gore, is sparse, though the short scene of nudity to which we are treated leaves us wanting more.Overall, though the film presents some interesting gore and a deliciously lurid back story for its antagonist, this new version ultimately fails to attain the general sense of depravity its makers presumably intended -- its graphic set pieces often undermined by pedestrian direction and a predictable script. Nonetheless, the sticky, squishy special-effects, the Court-TV-like back story, and the sexy women on display should satisfy real horror fans.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Violence and Gore</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Black Christmas (2006) uncut U.S. version *** (out of 4) Incredibly violent and rather trashy remake of Bob Clark's 1974 classic does what any remake should do; it offers us something new. The basic storyline is still in place but this remake goes for a totally different approach to the subject matter and with all the insane violence in this film it's really no wonder there was so much protest when this was released last Christmas. The story is pretty simply as a group of college girls are in their house and are eventually picked off one by one. There's no doubt that the 1974 version is a better made movie that features better director and better acting but style is not what this remake went for. Instead of style and atmosphere this remake gives us non-stop violence, which is so gory and over the top that you can help enjoy it on that level. Yes, there are many plot holes here as new characters are introduced by for a slasher film this pretty much delivers all the goods. The one interesting change to this film is that we see flashbacks of what happened to the killer when he was a child. At first I didn't know what these scenes were trying to do but they add to a few plot twists that make them worth watching. There are several references to the first film including the rocking chair and the attic as well as references to various other early slashers. The film also takes a very strong hatred feel towards religion and Christmas as there are several scenes talking bad about the two and other scenes where statues of Jesus are shown falling and various other things. I'm not sure how much of the violence made it into the theatrical version but this uncut version is pretty damn brutal with some incredibly graphic violence (including some to kids) and a sexual situation that I won't spoil since it's part of a plot change. Again, if you want a classy horror film then stick with the original. If you just want an old fashioned slasher with a pinch of a Euro giallo then this film is right up your alley.</fullReview>

		<date>2011-12-19</date>
		<username>happyendingrocks</username>
		<score>0.4</score>
		<shortDescription>Ho Ho Holy crap, this movie is awful</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Devoid of suspense or any real scares to speak of, this ill-advised update of Black Christmas is a remake in name only. While generous dollops of bloodshed are tacked on to fill the void left by the absence of anything resembling horror, the end result is a yuletide mess, and genre fans hoping for a film worthy of sharing a double feature with their annual screening of Silent Night, Deadly Night won't find a present worth opening here.A big schism erupts within the first five minutes of the movie, where we see our first buxom victim meet her fate just before we cut to a mental hospital, where we are given the back-story of a lunatic named Billy, who killed and ate his mother a ways back and who still tries to escape the asylum every December so that he can "be home for Christmas." Since we're fairly certain this particular homicidal maniac doesn't have the ability to telepathically murder boozing co-eds from inside his cell, the presence of a second killer is spelled out right off the bat.The film attempts to assert its intelligence via philosophical expoundings about the "neo-pagan magic" inherent in Christmas rituals, but since this conversation occurs among a group of stereotypical, bubble-headed sorority girls, these deep explorations are a definite credibility strain. Even better, the wizened lass who dispenses this profound wisdom proves herself an even more accomplished scholar five minutes later, when she talks her sorority sisters out of getting in touch with the cops after the victims-to-be receive a phone call in which a deranged man vows to kill them all. It's also important to note that this sage-like siren soon gets so drunk that she projectile vomits and passes out.As more details of Billy's back-story emerge, the film becomes even more implausible and downright icky. We eventually learn that the sorority residence is actually the house where Billy murdered his ghastly mother, and that not only have the co-eds come to terms with this brutal piece of their dwelling's history, they actually include the ostensibly institutionalized Billy in their Secret Santa gift exchange. We also get a thoroughly tasteless flashback which informs us that Billy and his mother had incestuous sex that produced an inbred daughter. Once all the facts are revealed, the whole plot is pretty much cut and dry, and Black Christmas doesn't even bother to attempt any twists, so any chance of us being surprised by the outcome of this tepid tale effectively end right there.I'm not sure if this is the product of lazy script-writing or of a misogynistic undercurrent, but despite their repeated assertions that they are sorority "sisters," the slasher-bait nymphettes in Black Christmas seem to loathe each other nearly as much as the killers do. This group of ladies call each other "b****" so often that I can honestly say I don't remember the names of any of the interchangeable characters who get sleigh-ed (ha!) along the way. Not to be outdone, the vaguely suspect boyfriend of our main heroine manages to drop the phrase "f***ing b*****s" about 8 times in one scene. I agree that "fornicating female dogs" would have been a tad wordy, but the screenwriters could of at least changed it up a bit for us.The film offers up a few nifty gore gags to keep us from falling asleep, but the killers' repeated use of holiday-themed weaponry eventually becomes so silly that it dilutes the impact of the money moments. No matter how gleefully the splatter is poured on, after watching various victims get strangled with Christmas lights, stabbed with candy canes, chopped with ice skates, gouged with conveniently pointy ornaments, and impaled with icicles, I ended up wondering who was going to get trampled by a reindeer, then found myself slightly disappointed when this never came to pass. Although, I will give the film credit for Billy's ghoulish "Christmas cookies," which can be held directly responsible for most of the stars I gave this movie.Ever since Scream so adeptly parodied the tropes of the classic slasher film, modern day splatter movies have wisely attempted to stray outside these confines. This is not the case with Black Christmas, which opts instead to take a huge leap back in time. The hapless victims here practically invite their demises, and their dumb decisions throughout make it nearly impossible to root them on. One duo meets their predictable ends when they decide that driving on snow-clogged roads through a blinding blizzard is safer than sticking with the group and waiting for help to come. Other bravo choices include climbing up into the attic to confront the killers once the survivors ascertain that's where the murderers are hiding, and the flight of one particularly hysterical gal, who eschews the neon "Exit" sign in front of her and chooses to retreat into a bedroom when being chased by one of the malevolent stalkers. Shockingly, her attempt to instead jump out of a second story window does not prove fruitful.The brazenly stupid denouement tacked on after the "final" confrontation with the killers only serves to pad the run time, and since you'll be wishing this thing was over already at that point, the conclusion to this fiasco is about as satisfying as unwrapping a pair of slipper socks.Black Christmas isn't unwatchable, but it's certainly pointless, and with decades of horror films at the discerning viewer's disposal, there's a really long list of offerings genre fans should cross off before they settle for this gimmicky and misguided dud. I don't want to over-do it with the holiday puns, but this movie practically begs for them, and when I finally made it to the end credits, the words "lump of coal" definitely came to mind.</fullReview>
	</review>

Ultimately, this is pretty much an assembly-line killing flick with no real value beyond a couple of nice racks, but it's got enough of a quality look to it that it's worth a 5-for-$5 rental at Blockbuster. 		<shortDescription>Nice try, but not that great.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>I knew this new remake of the 1974 classic, Black Christmas would hardly be decent. Well, it IS decent, but it's far from the hair raising original.My hopes got higher when I heard of the cast. I must admit that the cast is spectacular. Glen Morgan has rounded up a cast of the most beautiful and talented youth actresses in the industry. Katie Cassidy, Mary Elizabeth Winstead, Crystal Lowe, Lacey Chabert, Michelle Tratchenberg, and veteran funny lady Andrea Martin(who played Phyll in the original)headline the cast.However hard they try, the competent cast can't overcome the overall silliness of the movie. The narrative lacks the terror of the original. There is no suspense and besides a few jump scares, it's virtually scareless.The deaths are ridiculously over the top. The opening goes over well, with a nice update of Clair(Leela Savasta)'s death from the original. However, as the film progresses, the deaths get dumber and dumber, climaxing in an awful finale. It really is one of the most pathetic climaxes I've seen in a long time, completely lacking thrills. The only good moment comes from a sly homage to Happy Birthday To Me, in the form of a Christmas tree surrounded by the corpses of the girls.I know a good film was in here, and apparently, I'm right. The script was re-written many times, not to mention the many re-shoots and test screenings that managed to mess the movie up royally.I'll give it points for trying and being entertaining. Some of the comedy is good too. Wait for an uncut DVD!</fullReview>

		<username>ChiefGoreMongral</username>
		<score>0.5</score>
		<shortDescription>Gore Mongral's Movie Reviews: Black Christmas (2006)</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Black Christmas tells the tale of Billy a killer that has gotten loose from his sanitarium to kill some young ladies who are now living in the house he lived in up until his arrest. We are shown through flashbacks that are throughout the first half why Billy is the way he is and why he continues to do what he does. We also have our attractive young cast as well as a cast member from the original Black Christmas (Andrea "SCTV" Martin) playing the role of the dorm mother who all in one way or another end up being fodder for Billy and his homicidal rages.The original Black Christmas is a solid Slasher from the 70's that does a better job as a whole compared to the new movie, especially the twisted phone calls made by Billy, the new version just cannot match it in tone or bizarreness. However what it lacks in those areas in makes up for in raw carnage as this movie has some nice gore set pieces . There are some kills that if lingered on longer or shown in its entirety as oppose to just a bucket of red stuff being thrown on the ground simulating someone just got killed that would have made this an even more intense, for violence and gore sake, film.Make no mistake this film is not perfect as the story meanders in parts and only gives us side stories that go nowhere as well as a cast that you want to see die as most of them come off as preppy skanks!!! That's fine to me as no emotional attachment to the characters makes me want to see them die in a more violent way anyway. Also as in most Slashers we get the cast making stupid decisions in the least opportune times resulting, in most cases, their demise. For some the pacing will bother them as the beginning starts off well but in the middle a lot of nothing happens making way to a 20 minute free-for-all in the end that results in most of the cast dying in that short time frame.Taken in portions this film delivers for the most part as a Slasher but the average film fan will laugh this one off as a terrible movie or be too grossed out to watch the movie in its entirety. I would give this one a recommendation to Slasher fans even though this one has that modern teeny bopper feel in parts it makes up for it in its visceral kill sequences that I hope are extended on DVD. All other movie goers will want to see "Happy Feet" or some other festive movie.In closing go into this one with your Slasher hat on and nothing else and you should be mildly entertained. All others forget it: Score: 5/10: Average, A bland middle act hampers this one but fans of slasher films should find the kills are nice. Fans of Thrillers will not be amused as there is nothing thrilling here just out and out violence. All others will want to disregard this one. Here's hoping for an uncut DVD!!!</fullReview>

		<username>JR .</username>
		<score>0.5</score>
		<shortDescription>Dumb Fun</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>There's no conceptual thought process with a film like 'Black Christmas', but I'll be damned if I said the creators of 'Final Destination' didn't know how to make a stylish and entertaining picture. Despite its nice holiday set-up, the film is bogged down by its many clichés and plot holes. And while it's not scary in the least, the film gets points for offing characters in creative, and quite funny, ways. Another throw-away slasher, but one that'll keep your attention and may leave you somewhat satisfied.It's Christmastime, and a group of sorority sisters are celebrating the best way they know how, bickering and exchanging Secret Santa gifts. And every year, there's one present under the tree addressed to Billy, the reason why their house is now a legend. For fifteen years ago, Billy, who was abused by his mother and locked up in the attic, brutally murdered his mother and her boyfriend while sparing his sister... who also happens to be his daughter. It all happened here in the house the girls now stay in, and this year, Billy is coming home for the holidays. Home to his childhood house. Suddenly, the girls begin to receive a series of frightening and threatening phone calls from a mysterious caller that appears to be inside the house. Now, stranded in the middle of a winter storm, Alpha Kappa will begin to lose its members one by one in the grimmest ways possible.Written, produced, and directed by Glen Morgan, 'Black Christmas' is lucky it has style, because its villain is the antithesis of scary. And though there are some disturbing scenes, contained mainly in the film's flashbacks of Billy's upbringing, there's nothing in this film that would qualify as scary. You see one slasher, you've seen them all. Instead, 'Christmas' works on many of the same levels as the 'Final Destination' films, in the way they act as little more than elaborate death scenes one after the other. And hell, this may indeed be the goriest Christmas flick ever made, and that'll sure please the horror junkies. When all else fails, pile on the blood. Even when your film bends the rules of reality with gaping plot holes, a few buckets of blood will set things right. Right? The film's acting is what you'd expect, to be honest. A few talented actresses with a poor script to work with, but require less than the bulb that lights the scene. It is, however, nice to see Lacey Chabert back in action after lying low after her breakout performance in 'Mean Girls'. A fantastic actress, she just needs to find a script to suit her talent. The rest of the cast features many horror film vixens, including Katie Cassidy ('When A Stranger Calls'), Mary Elizabeth Winstead ('Final Destination 3'), Kristen Clock ('Final Destination'), Crystal Lowe ('Final Destination 3')and Andrea Martin, who starred in the original 1974 'Black Christmas'. Chabert and Michelle Trachtenberg are the lone horror virgins, but something tells me that won't last.If you're sick of the saccharine Christmas movies, and looking for something a bit more sac religious, 'Black Christmas' is a fairly safe bet. It's not a good movie by any standards, but acts as a nice diversion before you get back to your busy life. Just be aware of what you're getting yourself into, as you're not likely to find an ounce of originality in Morgan's latest fright(less) fest. If you're a fan of bad horror films, sit back and enjoy the ride. If not, stay away. Otherwise, you may lose your appetite for Christmas cookies.Review by Burtonesque, written for www.boxofficefanatic.com</fullReview>
	</review>
