		<shortDescription>"Goodbye Shirley" Indeed....</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Glen Morgan and James Wong gained notoriety by writing a few good episodes of the 90's TV sensation "The X-Files." Their later collaborative efforts on the show (notably, the episode "Kin") were not up to the same standards as their earlier work, but they soldiered on, running the show into the ground. Flash-forward to the the first decade in the 21st century and horror movie remakes have become an easy way for a studio to turn a buck. The Christmas holiday is a well-known "money" weekend for movies; people are stuck with little to do and often go see movies to relieve the boredom. Put "those guys who did stuff on X-Files" on a remake of a horror movie that is set during Christmas and release it on Christmas Eve....how could it go wrong, right? Well, it did go wrong and it pulls the X-Files legacy down with it.Morgan and Wong produced this mess and Morgan "wrote" the script and directed the movie, which is just sad. Fans of the X-Files will notice a similar feel in certain scenes, but any similarity ends at the visual level as this movie is a poorly executed mess. You will also notice several homages to the X-Files: the yellow-skinned antagonist being one, the obsession with eye injury being another and finally, the in-breeding. What is it with Morgan and Wong and inbreeding? Regardless, "Black Christmas" is an ugly, boring mess that grinds on inexorably to its conclusion. It's a shame that a cast filled with talented, gorgeous young women like Katie Cassidy, Michelle Trachentenberg and Mary Elizabeth Winstead have no better lines than "F___ Christmas!" and "Christmas sucks!" but I guess that's what happens when a movie is churned out by two guys who hit their stride with "Jose Chung's from Outer Space" and that was....what? 1997?</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Forgettable and poorly written slasher remake</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>On the last day before winter break, a sorority house comes under attack by a pair of mysterious assailants with a strange obsession for plastic bags and eye gouging.What's there to say about this disappointing stinker that hasn't been said a hundred times before. Even without comparing it to the original, it's bad. Other than a select few elements, there's not much good to say about this flick. Those few good elements would be. . . well. . . few and far between, to say the least. For one, the soundtrack was good, but it's hard to ruin Christmas carols. Also, the cast is extremely lot. Lacey Chabert, Michelle Trachtenberg, Katie Cassidy, etc., all look very fine indeed. And, I suppose the last positive would be some okay gore (especially the cookie-eating scene). From there on, it's all pretty bad. The writing is absolutely atrocious with almost every little detail and secret being explained more than the plan of a Bond villain. The change of Billy to some kind of liver-diseased weirdo was a big mistake. On two other technical notes, the acting is pretty bad, but not completely horrible; and, the direction is fairly mediocre, as it doesn't look TOO bad, but is certainly nothing to brag about. A truly annoying problem I had with the film was the lack of differentiation between the characters. Sure, you had some basic personalities (the drunk, the partygirl, the Christian, the weirdo), but they all kinda blend together and really have no true separation. I'm not sure if I even remember any of their names (except Eve, and that's only because I like the name). In the end, Black Christmas is a subpar, poorly made, and ultimately forgettable slasher that can easily be dismissed for the original (or anything else).Obligatory Christmas-Horror Elements:- Subgenre: Slasher- Christmas Carols: One of the few good things about the film: The holiday soundtrack.- Snow: Yeah, and icicles play a bit of a role.- Person in a Santa suit: People randomly show up in Santa outfits. . . not used very well though.- Violence/Gore: The deaths are repetitive to start, then over-the-top-stupid for the rest of the time. Lots of eye gouging and plastic bags.- Sex/Nudity: Not nearly enough to save the film. You get a bit of nudity and an occasional unsatisfying sex scene, but that's all.- Scares/Suspense: None. It tries, but fails completely.- Mystery: Again, it tries, but fails.- - -Final verdict: 3/10. Pass! -AP3-</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Actually, far more exciting than the 1974 original!</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Long time since I've been totally thrilled by a remake (the last one was "Dawn of the Dead"). I didn't expect much of another rehash of a so-called 1970s "classic", but -I don't know exactly why- I was curious about this one. Not precisely because I looooved so much the Bob Clark's first version. On the contrary, I estimated it had not exploited its potential to its limits. In fact, as I watched it, I even had this uncomfortable feeling of witnessing a disorderly made blueprint of Carpenter's "Halloween". Which made it interesting enough at the time, though. But quite unsatisfying... Here, in the 2006 version, I did not even have the time to think too much about what I had to expect or not. The film just made the deal right away. I particularly love the way the script did not care much in making its female characters too cute. In fact, most of the girls are actually plain bitches. Which made them the more lovable to me, surprisingly enough. Secondly, the killer character's background is told in a series of flashbacks included quite smoothly into the whole storytelling. The different elements are given in a very skillful way. No heavy-handed explanation as we had to get along with in the dreadful Rob Zombie's Halloween. Then, the plot itself grows suspenseful each minutes in a excellently orchestrated crescendo. Not a minute, the viewer feels cheated by twists and turns overblown or artificial. On top of that, the film is filled with original ideas to surprise the audience and play with its expectation. A very intelligent film made out of a tired ingredients (the killer chasing girls again and again), I simply loved its sarcastic tone, its terrifying use of innocent Christmas musics, its own score, the atmosphere, its fast pace, its sharp dialogs... everything. What can I say? I loved it, and yet I consider myself a very difficult moviegoer.For those who would want to know if i share the same values, here is the list of remakes I simply hated: Rob Zombie's Halloween, Amityville, The Fog, When a Stranger Calls, Texas Chainsaw Massacre, ... in fact almost all of them. Except "Dawn of the Dead" and, of course, "Black Christmas"!!!</fullReview>

		<username>MARIO GAUCI (marrod@melita.com)</username>
		<score>0.1</score>
		<shortDescription>BLACK Christmas (Glen Morgan, 2006) BOMB</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>I'm an admirer of the 1974 original, so it was out of mere curiosity that I decided to check out this remake. Several classic shockers of the 1970s have been revamped of late ? I've watched THE Texas CHAINSAW MASSACRE (2003) and, most recently, HALLOWEEN (2007); those two were nowhere near as good as the earlier films, but each had its points of interest. The same, however, cannot be said about the second version of BLACK Christmas. It is, easily, one of the worst films of its kind that I've come across; by changing a lot of the structure of the original, with it go a good many of its strong points ? and the end result is hardly recognizable, let alone necessary: in short, a real travesty!Perhaps the greatest coup of Bob Clark's original film was that we knew very little about the killer; in fact, we don't even get to see him except for his peering eyes. Here, on the other hand, everything is clumsily spelt out: from Billy's backstory involving a typically miserable childhood to the revelation of having two maniacs ? the other being Agnes, a character only fleetingly mentioned in the earlier film (the script, in fact, seems to have been concocted after one too many viewings of both HALLOWEEN [1978; which, ironically, was initially conceived as a sequel to the original BLACK Christmas] and CHINATOWN [1974]!). Also, one of the most disquieting elements about the earlier film ? the obscene phone calls ? are not only downplayed here but have been replaced with the dim-witted repetition of the line "She's my family now".Besides, the Police ? represented in the original by John Saxon ? or the character played in it by Keir Dullea, boyfriend of the female lead (the setting is a sorority house) and who is suspected of being behind the crime spree, barely register here. In the same vein, the girls themselves remain an anonymous bunch (as opposed to, say, Olivia Hussey and Margot Kidder from the 1974 film) ? which doesn't help audience identification any. Incidentally, Andrea Martin ? who played one of the victims in the original BLACK Christmas ? appears here as the house mother (whereas Bob Clark himself figured among the remake's myriad producers!).</fullReview>
	</review>

		<username>Coventry</username>
		<score>0.2</score>
		<shortDescription>Jingle Bells, This Movie Smells ...</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Okay, the popular concept of remaking classic horror milestones is not exactly the best cinema-trend in history and the attempts more than often result in dreadful movies. But are some of the nowadays directors, like Glen Morgan, really so frustrated about their own lack of talent that they deliberately want to damage the good reputation of an entire genre and its acclaimed classics? "Black Christmas 2006" is a tremendous insult to "Black Christmas 1974", particularly because that latter was such an influential and important film. The new version is wildly over-the-top and extremely incoherent in the scripting department, the film hangs together by sickening &amp; gory set pieces, the acting performances are embarrassing and every effort to bring depth or build up tension either makes no sense or goes nowhere. The plot is no longer a compelling whodunit, but a rudimentary and utterly brainless stalk-and-slash turkey. On Christmas evening, a frat house full of whiny &amp; spoiled girl students becomes the target of escaped raving lunatic killer Billy Lenz. For you see, this was the house where Billy's battle-axe mother killed his beloved father, locked him up in the attic for years and even raped him. Every year around Christmas Billy threatens to get home for the holidays, but this year he's dead serious and the girls will physically experience this. I think we've established that "Black Christmas 2006" is an phenomenally retarded film and that every die-hard fan of the original should avoid it in order to avoid a nervous breakdown, but does this updated version has absolutely nothing to offer then? Well yes actually, it features a lot (and I do mean A LOT) of gory massacres and filthy make-up effects. I didn't even think it was possible, but this film almost exaggerates in being sick-spirited, exploitative and gratuitously sadistic. Billy Lenz seemingly has an awkward fascination for gaging out people's eyeballs and every act of torture is shown in great detail. So, if you have an incontrollable passion for watching screaming &amp; helpless young girls getting mutilated, this is your movie. Then there's also the oddest incestuous sub plot I ever beheld, the inevitably clichéd reasons for characters not being able to use their mobile phones and the absence of a strong lead character. The strangest thing of all remains that Bob Clark, director of the fabulous original, actually produced this dud! Not a bad word about Clark, also because he passed away earlier this year, but why would he contribute to a travesty that desperately imitates his own work? Another weird detail is that Glen Morgan was already responsible for the remake "Willard", and that actually is a pleasingly grim and atmosphere-driven film.</fullReview>

		<score>0.1</score>
		<shortDescription>Worst. Remake. Ever.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Surely no one sets out to make a bad movie. But in the case of the Black Christmas remake, it's hard to imagine writer/director Glen Morgan honestly thinking that this was the best he could do. The original Black Christmas is a classic, a forerunner to the modern slasher movie - stylish and eery and unsettling. But most importantly, simple and straight forward. A slasher and a murder mystery, deftly directed by Bob Clark. The remake (WHY!?) is, to be blunt, absolutely dreadful. From the first frame to the pitiful end, Black Christmas (2006) puts its viewer through the ringer, from the absurd and outlandish to the just plain dull and stupid. Giving the killer an elaborate (and ridiculous) backstory is beside the point, meaningless, mere filler. We get lame attempts at humor and gross out moments that are bad camp. The inclusion of Billy's sister, Agnes, is so out-of-left-field that it feels like Morgan was simply trying to throw in a few extra kills and pad out the movie's already spare running time. The movie isn't even 90 minutes, but you feel every second, particularly with the completely unnecessary hospital finale dragging things out to an asinine, but blessed close. Fans of the original Black Christmas should feel insulted. Horror fans should feel taken advantage of. The human race as a whole should shudder knowing this slag of trash came from one of its own. We can only hope this movie will end the careers of all involved.</fullReview>

		<fullReview>I can't believe that some people out there actually enjoyed this film. It's yet another pointless, witless remake of an original which, though not brilliant, was genuinely unsettling and still memorable many years after viewing. This cheapo quickie, by contrast, has been thrown together without imagination or talent. The writer-director has either never seen a proper slasher movie or has simply failed to grasp what makes them work.The movie disappoints on every level. It introduces a laboured backstory for the killer, but makes the sorority girls so one-dimensional that you literally cannot tell them apart, let alone care what happens to them. The killer's predilection for gouging out eyeballs is unpleasant-nasty rather than scary-nasty, and is an inadequate, low-budget substitute for the great Tom Savini SFX of yore. You need only compare Black Christmas 2006 with the best of the 80s slasher pics (probably Joseph Zito's The Prowler, which really goes for it), or the brilliant recent women-in-peril chiller The Descent, to realise just how woefully inadequate this film is. The only compensation is the short running time - and even at 84 minutes, the damn thing seems to drag.</fullReview>

Lots of eye gouging gore and the return of original cast member Andrea Martin, now playing the house mother of the sorority. I was surprised how the writers made this into a Christmas version of "Halloween", even down to the killer's theme music. If you want a fun horror movie that doesn't take itself too seriously, but is worth the $7.50 admissions price, go see this before it leaves theaters.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>You Could Do a Lot Worse; You could Be Watching the Original</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Somebody thought it was time to dust off the rights to the cultish, dreary Black Christmas from 1974 and give it a fresh coat of paint. The results are underwhelming but it's still an improvement. A creepy, fun backstory is now in place, explaining the gruesome mayhem and the film-makers have provided a satisfying conclusion; something the 1974 version couldn't be bothered with. The cast is bright and game for the material and the director has a knack for horror which we all know from having enjoyed series like The X Files and the Final Destination franchise. There's enough gore and suspense to please fans of the genre but there's also a sense that this one was derailed by studio tampering. Could be better, could be worse. But it's a step up from the Bob (Porky's) Clark version.</fullReview>

		<date>2007-11-28</date>
		<username>Paul Andrews (poolandrews@hotmail.com)</username>
		<score>0.6</score>
		<shortDescription>"Take a look outside, it's raining hail the size of Santa's ball sack." I quite liked it.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Black Christmas is set in a sorority house called Alpha Kappa on Christmas eve, a house where Billy Lenz (Robert Mann) used to live several years ago &amp; where he murdered his abusive mum (Karin Konoval) &amp; his stepfather (Howard Seigel) as well as mutilating his sister Agnes (Dead Friss). The house mother Mrs. Mac (Andrea Martin) has organised lots of presents for her girls like Kelli (Katie Cassidy), however the girls start to receive disturbing phone calls &amp; mysteriously begin to disappear. Has a vengeful Billy returned home to continue his killing spree? Will any of the girls survive to see the new year...This Canadian American co-production was written, co-produced &amp; directed by Glen Morgan &amp; is a remake of the original Black Christmas (1974) in a growing list of classic horror flicks which have been remade by Hollywood in recent years like The Hills Have Eyes (2006) &amp; Halloween (2007). First of all I will openly admit right now that I have not seen the original Black Christmas, although I do actually have the special edition on DVD I haven't got round to seeing it yet so bear that in mind. Secondly Black Christmas is one of those frustrating films which exist in several different versions, the 'R' rated &amp; 'Unrated' American cuts &amp; the almost completely different European cut which has a different ending, different kill scenes &amp; there are even character's in each version which don't appear in the other (Kelli's parents, the morgue attendant for instance) so everyone bear in mind I will be basing my comment on the European version. Got that? Good. The script is at heart nothing more than a teen slasher flick, the basic message is if you like your slasher films then there's a fair chance you'll like Black Christmas on some level &amp; if you don't like teen slasher films then you probably won't like Black Christmas &amp; I honestly think that essentially is what it boils down to. The character's are painted in rather broad stereotypical strokes but they serve their purpose well enough &amp; are no worse than any other slasher flick. I liked the lengthy flashback scenes back to Billy's childhood &amp; the horror he suffered at the hands of his mother, it came as a nice break from the standard teen scenes &amp; they were pretty gross in their own right with strong references of incest. Speaking of which there's some cool gore in Black Christmas (remember I'm commenting on the UK version) &amp; some great kills. On the down side the film isn't anything particularly groundbreaking, the revelation of the killers could have been better &amp; it's a bit predictable. I mean the killings started before Billy even escaped so as a potential red herring he was wasted &amp; as a result so was the opportunity for a surprise twist ending.Director Morgan does a good job, there's obviously plenty of Christmas decorations hung up everywhere &amp; the film has a nice horror film atmosphere. It's entirely at night as a fierce snowstorm rages outside. As already mentioned the UK version contains some good gore, eyes are plucked out, icicles are impaled in people's heads, there's plenty of blood splashed around, someone makes some Christmas cookies out of ripped off skin, there are a couple of decapitated heads, eyeballs are eaten &amp; I love the scene when there's lots of eyeballs hanging on a Christmas tree like ball-balls! I've actually seen the US ending &amp; there's a scene where someone is impaled on a Christmas tree which is cool &amp; more generally the ending is clearer on the US cut. Strangely &amp; maybe somewhat disappointingly there's no nudity other than a girls bare bum.With a supposed budget of about $9,000,000 Black Christmas is well made with that big Hollywood studio polish to it. The score contains many traditional Christmas carol's used in sinister situations. Shot on location in Vancouver in British Columbia in Canada apparently in a 29 day shoot although there were re-shoots. The acting is alright, all the girls are very good looking &amp; easy on the eye which helps. Andrea Martin played Phyllis in the original Black Christmas.Black Christmas '06 is, in my opinion, a pretty good remake of the '74 original that I actually rather enjoyed. It's nothing amazing but I liked it &amp; it's as simple &amp; straight forward as that. However this gets a lot of stick &amp; a lot of people don't seem to like it so maybe I'm in the minority, but then again I don't care.</fullReview>
